<div id="review_191915671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191915671" />
    <a title="Cici" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1931122-cici"><img alt="Cici" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354803345p2/1931122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191915671?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cici" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cici" href="/user/show/1931122-cici">Cici</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1931122-cici?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191915671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7304600877606913072">I've come to realize why I am addicted to these types of books, for years I've had nightmares about the world ending or some kind of disaster where I'm trying to save my kids and sometimes other people. I do know that I have these nightmares when I am stressed out and overwhelmed and that's what the dream is symbolizing(something in my life is out of control) and me trying to save people symbolizes that I'm trying to get it under control. I used to be huge into dreams and their meanings. But, st</span>
  <span id="freeText7304600877606913072" style="display:none">I've come to realize why I am addicted to these types of books, for years I've had nightmares about the world ending or some kind of disaster where I'm trying to save my kids and sometimes other people. I do know that I have these nightmares when I am stressed out and overwhelmed and that's what the dream is symbolizing(something in my life is out of control) and me trying to save people symbolizes that I'm trying to get it under control. I used to be huge into dreams and their meanings. But, still these dreams are so real and scary that I will think about them for days. It also terrifies me that this could really happen to me and my loved ones. So, I guess reading these types of books gives me a little hope that we could survive, as crazy as that may seem.<br /><br />Life as we knew it, wow, it's pretty amazing. When I first started reading it I thought it was just ok(before all the action started) but then it had this snowball affect and just kept getting better and better and better. I'm impressed at where this author has taken me and all the emotions I felt along the way. When these characters were starving, I couldn't even eat, that's how attached I felt to these characters. When Miranda bursts into laughter after hysteria and panic, I totally get it, I've had these same emotions plenty.<br /><br />This story is told thorugh Miranda's diary. Miranda is a 16-year old normal girl, who lives with her mother and two brothers. <br /><br />She's been writing about her family, her friends, interests, homework and all the excitement over the meteor that's going to be hitting the moon. <br /><br />When this huge meteor hits the moon it knocks the moon out of orbit and causes a lot of world disasters. Tsunamis are hitting everywhere and then there's crazy storms and soon volcanic erruptions and volcanic ash covering the world, servere climate changes, states are just gone, submerged under water. So many people have died and the ones still alive are struggling to survive.<br /><br />Stores are being ransacked, gasoline prices are crazy unbelievable(like $75 for 3 gallons of gas), electricity is almost non-existent and it's a matter of time before food and water runs out. <br /><br />The main characters are strong and also very normal, family-next-door type. The kids grow up pretty quickly and learn to make sacrifices and value life.<br /><br />This book really makes you appreciate the little things and important things in life.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7304600877606913072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1417281664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1417281664" />
    <a title="Biz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24240418-biz"><img alt="Biz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562553192p2/24240418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1417281664?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Biz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Biz" href="/user/show/24240418-biz">Biz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24240418-biz?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24240418-biz?shelf=recs-strong-women">recs-strong-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24240418-biz?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24240418-biz?shelf=all-time-favorite-standalones">all-time-favorite-standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24240418-biz?shelf=five-star">five-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24240418-biz?shelf=recs-books-that-will-make-you-cry">recs-books-that-will-make-you-cry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1417281664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3173232534744252515"><blockquote>
  <i>”I didn’t start this diary for it to be a record of death.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>CHILLS. That’s what I feel every time I read this book. Straight. Up. <b>
  <i>chills.</i>
</b> <br/><br/><i>Life as We Knew It</i> is unique to other apocalypse books I’ve read, and that makes it even more enjoyable. It’s different because there isn’t really a lot of action at all. The only action/excitement there is happens in the first fifty pages. After that, you just get to see Miranda’s world slowly shrink as things become unsafe, or it’s too cold or she’s t</span>
  <span id="freeText3173232534744252515" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>”I didn’t start this diary for it to be a record of death.”</i>
</blockquote><br />CHILLS. That’s what I feel every time I read this book. Straight. Up. <b>
  <i>chills.</i>
</b> <br /><br /><i>Life as We Knew It</i> is unique to other apocalypse books I’ve read, and that makes it even more enjoyable. It’s different because there isn’t really a lot of action at all. The only action/excitement there is happens in the first fifty pages. After that, you just get to see Miranda’s world slowly shrink as things become unsafe, or it’s too cold or she’s too hungry, and she has to <b>watch her loved ones die off one by one</b>. <br /><br />Horror and terror are different – horror has a lot of jump scares and makes your heart race, but terror is that sinking slow-burn scariness that stays with you long after you’re done. <i>Life As We Knew It</i> is definitely a terror book. Because here’s the thing: you can actually <i>see</i> in your mind all the stuff in this book happening, and in the rest of the series it gets even more terrifyingly realistic. This book (and series) really has a good grip on human condition, not to mention the evils, and sometimes good, that humans are capable of. That’s what makes it all the more scary.<br /><br />The nightmares that Miranda has throughout this book also add to the scary factor. She goes from having nightmares about heaven and not being let in, to nightmares of hell, to disorienting nightmares in which she sees her perished or unknown-fated loved ones having fun without her. <br /><br />This book also has some really strong messages that emphasize on family, gratefulness, and perseverance, but it’s never preachy or glorified. It’s terrifying and really sad, yes, but there’s also a lot of hope, which makes the sad parts easier to read. <br /><br />I’ve read this book SO many times and I’ve just started to notice all the little intricacies that went into it. At the beginning of the book, when Miranda is doubtful that anything <i>truly</i> bad is going to happen, she says a lot of “I’ll never” statements, but as time goes on, she rescinds each and every one of those statements as she lowers her pride and does what it takes to survive. It's terrifying and awe-inspiring and just. Wow.<br /><br />There is just something incredibly unsettling about this book, and it's hard to describe, but whenever you talk to someone else who's read it they just GET it and it's just. Hard to explain. It's a book you have to experience.<br /><br />It just blows me away how smoothly this book progresses. There is so much showing and so little telling in this book, and usually the changes are so subtle that you don’t even notice them happening. I’m pretty sure I’ve read this at least five times and I still can’t tell you when the electricity shuts off for good, or when the characters stop listening to the radio. <br /><br />All in all, definitely my favorite apocalypse book of all time, and one of my very all-time favorite books. It’s intense, gritty, and will make you cry (and make you want to invest in food storage). <br /><blockquote>
  <i>”I don’t even know why I’m writing this down, except that I feel fine and maybe tomorrow I’ll be dead. And if that happens, and someone should find my journal, I want them to know what happened. <br /><br />We are a family. We love each other. We’ve been scared together and brave together. If this is how it ends, so be it. <br /><br />Only, please, don’t let me be the last one to die.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3173232534744252515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71273424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12250796233950539480">I usually really enjoy a dystopian post-apoclyptic novel more than most, but this one left me cold on several fronts.<br/><br/>The basic gist of the story is an asteroid hits the moon and causes immense changes to the teenage heroine's lifestyle.<br/><br/>Issue 1: not enough mayhem ensues with the events in the story. I would easily expect more looting and depravity in this type of scenario. Everything seemed too put together. For example, the coastal regions are decimated ... yet internet access is still available</span>
  <span id="freeText12250796233950539480" style="display:none">I usually really enjoy a dystopian post-apoclyptic novel more than most, but this one left me cold on several fronts.<br /><br />The basic gist of the story is an asteroid hits the moon and causes immense changes to the teenage heroine's lifestyle.<br /><br />Issue 1: not enough mayhem ensues with the events in the story. I would easily expect more looting and depravity in this type of scenario. Everything seemed too put together. For example, the coastal regions are decimated ... yet internet access is still available when power is working. Hmmmm...<br /><br /><br />Issue 2: too much teenager whining angst. Yes, this was a young adult book, but others I have read within the same genre were more sophisticated at telling the story from the perspective of the teenager without sounding like a contrived plot device.<br /><br /><br />Issue 3: there was a lot of anti-Christianity thoughts in this book. Characters that had any faith in their life were portrayed as weak and ignorant. It got old to me very quickly.<br /><br /><br />I still will likely read more in the series to see if anything changes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12250796233950539480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L1a44zFW80bN6ZGvkKeHiYMcefKGzyN9Or+xCdpuOqXMCkX6t3av4n2pEglVy+SxmKL+1F1jzc+18VlxqFbJAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X/SZILmYx3GGJboeeLPA1M4efk8GemzkVolzl1k9hsm8qGQ5P7ib1TZlObi936Ps1aD5ad3WglbZx5vvKwV1bw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11746333212271871279">Susan Beth Pfeffer was born in New York City in 1948. She grew up in the city and its nearby suburbs and spent summers in the Catskill Mountains. When she was six her father wrote and published a book on constitutional law, and Pfeffer decided that she, too, wanted to be a writer. That year she wrote her first story, about the love between an Oreo cookie and a pair of scissors. However, it wasn't </span>
  <span id="freeText11746333212271871279" style="display:none">Susan Beth Pfeffer was born in New York City in 1948. She grew up in the city and its nearby suburbs and spent summers in the Catskill Mountains. When she was six her father wrote and published a book on constitutional law, and Pfeffer decided that she, too, wanted to be a writer. That year she wrote her first story, about the love between an Oreo cookie and a pair of scissors. However, it wasn't until 1970 that her first book, Just Morgan, was published. She wrote it during her last semester at New York University; since then, she has been a full-time writer for young people. <br /><br />She has won numerous awards and citations for her work, which range from picture books to middle-grade and young-adult novels, and include both contemporary and historical fiction. She is also the author of the popular Portraits of Little Women series for grades 3-6, and has written a book for adults on writing for children.<br /><br />To date, she has written more than 60 books. About David was awarded the South Carolina Young Adult Book Award. The Year Without Michael is an ALA Best Book for Young Adults and winner of the South Carolina Young Adult Book Award; it was also named by the American Library Association as one of the hundred best books for teenagers written between 1968-1993. <br /><br />When she is not working, she enjoys watching movies, both new and old, and collecting movie memorabilia, reading biographies and histories, and eating foods that are bad for her. She lives in Middletown, New York, with her two cats, Alexander and Emily.<br /><br />Named the American Library Associations Young Adult Library Services Association Best Book for Young Adults 2007 and Teens’ Top Ten Booklist in 2007. Finalist for the Andre Norton Award, Quill Awards, Hal Clement Awards</span>
  <a data-text-id="11746333212271871279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
